<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 245; left: 39; width: 719; height: 
60"><b>MEDIA RELEASE:   </b></DIV>
<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 279; left: 40; width: 718; height: 
203"><font style="line-height:16px;"><b>SIBANYE GOLD AMENDS THE TERMS OF ITS 
DEBT<br>
 <br>Westonaria,  11  July  2013:</b>  Sibanye  Gold  Limited  (JSE:  SGL  &amp;
NYSE:  SBGL)  today  announced  that  it  had <br>amended the terms and 
constraints of its Bridge Loan with its lenders. <br> <br>The previous Bridge 
Loan Facilities Agreement, concluded in November 2012, constrained Sibanye Gold 
<br>from paying an interim dividend in the financial year ending December 2013 
and limited a final dividend <br>to 25% of normalised earnings, provided Sibanye
Gold&#8216;s gross debt was not more than R4.0 billion after <br>paying a 
dividend.<br>
  <br>In  terms  of  the  new  amendments  made  to  the  Bridge  Loan  
Facilities  Agreement,  the  Sibanye  Gold <br>Board  of  Directors  may  now  
consider  an  interim  dividend  and  a  larger  final  dividend  in  respect  
of  the <br>financial year ending 31 December 2013, subject to the restrictions 
detailed below:  </font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:500;left:58">&#149;&nbsp;<FONT style="font-
family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
  </FONT>an interim dividend of up to 25% of normalised earnings in respect of 
its financial half year ended </DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:515;left:81"><font style="line-
height:16px;">on 30 June 2013, provided that Sibanye Gold&#8217;s net debt does 
not exceed R4.0 billion after such <br>dividend payment and the wage 
negotiations with organised labour have been concluded; and </font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:557;left:58">&#149;&nbsp;<FONT style="font-
family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
  </FONT>a  final  dividend  of  up  to  35%  of  normalised  earnings  (less  
any  interim  dividend  paid)  for  the </DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:572;left:81"><font style="line-
height:16px;">financial  year  ending on 31  December 2013,  provided  that  
Sibanye Gold&#8217;s  gross  debt  does not <br>exceed  R3.5  billion  after  
the  dividend  payment.    Alternatively  a  limited  final  dividend  of  25%  
of <br>normalised earnings (less any interim dividend paid), may be declared, 
provided that gross debt <br>does not exceed R4.0 billion after the dividend 
payment. </font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:638;left:35"><font style="line-height:16px;"> 
<br>The  Bridge  Loan  structure  will  still  reduce  to  R5.0  billion  on  
the  earliest  of;  the  date  on  which  Sibanye <br>Gold&#8217;s board of 
directors declare a final dividend in respect of the financial year ending 31 
December <br>2013,  or  on 18 February  2014,  but  the structure  of  the 
Facility  has now  been  amended  to a  R3.0  billion <br>revolving credit 
facility and a R3.0 billion term loan facility as opposed to the R2.0 billion 
revolving credit <br>facility and a R4.0 billion term loan facility before the
amendment.  <br> <br>Sibanye  Gold  is  currently  engaging  with  its  lenders 
to  extend  the  term  of  its  debt  and  will  update  the <br>market as soon 
as agreement has been reached.<br>
  <br>Neal Froneman, CEO of Sibanye Gold, said: &#8220;we are pleased that our 
lenders have agreed to relax the <br>constraint on paying an interim dividend 
and amended the terms of the Bridging Facilities. The revised  <br> 
</font></DIV>
</DIV>
</FONT><FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:8pt;color:#000000;"><DIV 
style="position:relative;width:758;height:1073;page-break-before:always;">
<IMG style="position:absolute;top:-2146;clip:rect(2146,758,3219,0)" 
src="sibanye_debt001n.gif" alt="background image">
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:39;left:35"><font style="font-size:12.8pt;"> 
</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:39;left:139"><font style="font-size:12.8pt;"> 
</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 103; left: 29; width: 729; height: 
109"><font style="line-height:16px;"> <br>terms  recognise  the  cash  
generative  ability  of  our  assets,  even  at  lower  prevailing  gold  prices
and  will <br>provide greater balance sheet flexibility and the ability to pay 
dividends to shareholders earlier&#8221;. <br> <br><b>Contact <br></b>James 
Wellsted <br>Head of Corporate Affairs <br>Sibanye Gold Limited <br>+27 83 453 
4014 <br>james.wellsted@sibanyegold.co.za <br> </font></DIV>
</DIV>

<DIV style="position:absolute;top:112;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;">Sibanye Gold Limited <br>Incorporated in the Republic of South 
Africa <br>Registration number 2002/031431/06 <br>Share code: SGL <br>ISIN 
&#8211; ZAE000173951 <br>Issuer code: SGL <br>(&#8220;Sibanye Gold&#8221; or 
&#8220;the Company&#8221;)</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:244;left:91 "><b>INITIAL RESTRUCTURING OF 
SIBANYE GOLD&#8217;S BRIDGING LOAN FACILITIES</b></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:277;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;"><b>Westonaria, 11 July 2013</b>: Sibanye Gold Limited (JSE: SGL 
&amp; NYSE: <br>SBGL) has reached agreement with the Lenders of its Bridge Loan 
<br>to amend the Bridge Loan Facilities Agreement. </font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:344;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;">In accordance with the Bridge Loan Facilities Agreement concluded 
<br>in November 2012, Sibanye Gold was not entitled to pay an interim 
<br>dividend in the financial year ending December 2013 and could <br>only 
declare and pay a final dividend of up to 25% of normalised <br>earnings, 
provided Sibanye Gold&#8216;s gross debt was not more than <br>R4.0 billion 
after such dividend payment.</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 451; left: 92; width: 666; height: 
99"><font style="line-height:16px;">In terms of the new amendments made to the 
Bridge Loan Facilities<br>Agreement, the Sibanye Gold Board of Directors may now
consider<br>an interim dividend and a larger final dividend in respect of 
the<br>financial year ending 31 December 2013, subject to the <br>restrictions 
detailed below. Sibanye Gold can now consider <br>declaring and 
paying:</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 562; left: 137; width: 601; height: 
75"><font style="line-height:16px;">&#149;
  an interim dividend of up to 25% of normalised earnings in <br></font><font 
style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
  </font><font style="line-height:16px;">respect of its financial half year 
ended on 30 June 2013, <br></font><font style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
  </font><font style="line-height:16px;">provided that Sibanye Gold&#8217;s net 
debt does not exceed R4.0 <br></font><font style="line-
height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
  </font><font style="line-height:16px;">billion after such dividend payment and
the wage <br></font><font style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</font><font style="line-height:16px;">negotiations with organised labour have
been concluded; and</font></DIV>
<DIV style="position: absolute; top: 660; left: 136; width: 622; height: 
108">&#149; a final dividend
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">
</FONT>of up to 35% of normalised earnings (less<FONT style="font-
family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">&nbsp;<br>
  &nbsp;&nbsp; </FONT><font style="line-height:16px;">any interim dividend paid)
in respect of its financial year <br></font>
  <font style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp; </font><font style="line-
height:16px;">ending on 31 December 2013, provided that Sibanye 
Gold&#8217;s<br></font>
  <font style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp; </font><font style="line-
height:16px;">gross debt does not exceed R3.5 billion after the dividend 
<br></font>
  <font style="line-height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp; </font><font style="line-
height:16px;">payment.</font>
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">
</FONT>Alternatively a final dividend limited to 25% of
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;">&nbsp;
</FONT><font style="line-height:16px;"><br>
  </font>
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;"><font style="line-
height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</font>
</FONT><font style="line-height:16px;">normalised earnings (less any interim 
dividend paid), may be <br></font>
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;"><font style="line-
height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</font>
</FONT><font style="line-height:16px;">declared, provided that gross debt does 
not exceed R4.0<br></font>
<FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:9pt;color:#000000;"><font style="line-
height:16px;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</font>
</FONT><font style="line-height:16px;">billion after the dividend 
payment.</font> </DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:798;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;">The structure of the Bridge Loan has also been amended, providing 
<br>Sibanye Gold with more flexibility and the opportunity to utilise <br>some 
of its cash to reduce its current debt position. The R6.0 <br>billion Bridge 
Loan structure now comprises of a R3.0 billion <br>revolving credit facility and
a R3.0 billion term loan facility<br>(before the amendment it was a R2.0 billion
revolving credit <br>facility and a R4.0 billion term loan facility). Both 
facilities <br>will reduce from R3.0 billion to R2.5 billion (resulting in debt 
<br>available to Sibanye Gold of R5.0 billion) on the earliest of;<br>the date 
on which Sibanye Gold&#8217;s board of directors declare a</font></DIV>
</DIV>
</FONT><FONT style="font-family:arial;font-size:8pt;color:#000000;"><DIV 
style="position:relative;width:758;height:1073;page-break-before:always;">
<IMG style="position:absolute;top:-4292;clip:rect(4292,758,5365,0)" 
src="sibanye_debt001n.gif" alt="background image">
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:94 ;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;">final dividend in respect of the financial year ending 
31<br>December 2013, or on 18 February 2014. </font></DIV>
<DIV style="position:absolute;top:144;left:91 "><font style="line-
height:16px;">Sibanye Gold is currently engaging with its lenders to extend the 
<br>term of its debt and will update the market as soon as agreement <br>has 
been reached. </font></DIV>
